  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_58fbf868-f198-40b3-80c0-1edc3bad3941'
      });

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1682549910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6807641634348387690"><b>I fully admit I was pretty bored reading this.</b> Ugh, my adoration for this series has seriously taken a downward spiral of doom AND I AM THE SADNESS. I'm really <i>really</i> keen for the finale book and the cliffhanger #11 just gave us (dangit cliffhangers ARGH). But ultimately I felt like this volume went <b>round and round in circles.</b> <br/><br/>• All of Near's deducing was stuff WE READERS ALREADY KNOW because we're in Light's head to. So it was seriously boring.<br/>• There was barely any Misa. Not that I love Misa..</span>
  <span id="freeText6807641634348387690" style="display:none"><b>I fully admit I was pretty bored reading this.</b> Ugh, my adoration for this series has seriously taken a downward spiral of doom AND I AM THE SADNESS. I'm really <i>really</i> keen for the finale book and the cliffhanger #11 just gave us (dangit cliffhangers ARGH). But ultimately I felt like this volume went <b>round and round in circles.</b> <br /><br />• All of Near's deducing was stuff WE READERS ALREADY KNOW because we're in Light's head to. So it was seriously boring.<br />• There was barely any Misa. Not that I love Misa...but at least she provides some comedy!<br />• THERE WAS BARELY ANY RYUK AND THIS IS UNACCEPTABLE.<br />• Mello was only on the last page, thank goodness. Mello and his pretty hair are a complete waste of space.<br />• I was just all around droopy eyed reading it and not overly engaged at all.<br />• The REAL problem is I don't even have a preference to who wins. I deduce it'll be Near, but with some plot twist (I HOPE) to keep things sparky. But otherwise...like, I don't really care about Near???? He's cute tho??? But that's it????<br />• Seriously though, THE ART IS ALWAYS A+++. I would buy this series just because it's so pretty.<br />• Everyone is pretty.<br />• I also hate freaking hate Light's womanising ways. Like someone hi five him in the face with a brick wall, please.<br />• I honestly should really just stop reading the series if I'm bored with it BUT THERE IS ONE MORE BOOK AND I AIN'T A QUITTER.<br />• I also thought it was <i>very</i> cute that Near was like "I'm going to Japan!" and then immediately "Please someone take me to Japan I don't want to fly alone"...hahhaha. SO ADORABLE OMG LITTLE CLEVER CHILD SHERLOCK CREATURE.<br />• (Although, like adorable is grand and all but it still doesn't make me overly root for him.)<br />• Light is basically a slimy grape though.<br />• It was also a very intense book with lots of looooong deducing conversations and both teams made some big breakthroughs so YEAH THERE'S THAT. But I found it wearying and repetitive, ultimately.<br />• Ugh. I'm tired. I need a cookie.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6807641634348387690" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13859549251596934493">Good set up for the final novel. As I get closer and closer to the end of the series, I'm becoming increasingly annoyed/amused at how women are depicted in this series. I realize it's a manga series aimed at boys, but come on. They're all either victims (see Light's sister), crazy/annoying/stupid (see Misa), or pathetically gullible (see Takada). Even the shinigami from a few volumes back that was supposed to be female was disappointing. Then again, perhaps I'm overthinking this. It is a teen bo</span>
  <span id="freeText13859549251596934493" style="display:none">Good set up for the final novel. As I get closer and closer to the end of the series, I'm becoming increasingly annoyed/amused at how women are depicted in this series. I realize it's a manga series aimed at boys, but come on. They're all either victims (see Light's sister), crazy/annoying/stupid (see Misa), or pathetically gullible (see Takada). Even the shinigami from a few volumes back that was supposed to be female was disappointing. Then again, perhaps I'm overthinking this. It is a teen boys' comic, after all.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Colleen Venable" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Colleen Venable" href="/user/show/61222-colleen-venable">Colleen Venable</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34097106" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7625735070525035594">Can I just say that Near's doll collection totally freaks me out! Why do they sort of but not really look like the characters? Eeeee. Why can't he go back to constantly playing with plastic ducks?! I find it funny that they felt the need to give Near and Mello these distinct personality ticks. If you ask me it holds their characters back a bit and venture more towards caricature. This might have been a 2 star rating if it wasn't for those last few pages. No even more than that—those last few pan</span>
  <span id="freeText7625735070525035594" style="display:none">Can I just say that Near's doll collection totally freaks me out! Why do they sort of but not really look like the characters? Eeeee. Why can't he go back to constantly playing with plastic ducks?! I find it funny that they felt the need to give Near and Mello these distinct personality ticks. If you ask me it holds their characters back a bit and venture more towards caricature. This might have been a 2 star rating if it wasn't for those last few pages. No even more than that—those last few panels. Totally knocked me away! I actually almost gave it 5 but then had to remind myself I had fallen asleep, nose first into the book spine, around page 20. Not a great sign. I am totally a Mello fan, even if I still think he should have been written as a female. Though I can't complain as much since Hal Linder is finally representing a smart strong woman in this book series, literally the first one we've come across in over 2,000 pages! Of course she IS a double-crosser and casually finds an excuse in the beginning to strip and shower while holding a conversation, but compared to the horrible representations of women in this whole series Linder is pretty darn bad-ass. Let's hope she plays a bigger role in the final two books. One that DOESN'T involve her falling in love or learn to make casserole or something. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7625735070525035594" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2582811379" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2582811379" />
    <a title="Britton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/86934326-britton"><img alt="Britton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547147480p2/86934326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2582811379?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Britton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Britton" href="/user/show/86934326-britton">Britton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86934326-britton?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86934326-britton?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86934326-britton?shelf=other-comic-companies">other-comic-companies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86934326-britton?shelf=books-i-ve-read-multiple-times">books-i-ve-read-multiple-times</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86934326-britton?shelf=books-that-have-moved-me">books-that-have-moved-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86934326-britton?shelf=books-you-should-really-check-out">books-you-should-really-check-out</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86934326-britton?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86934326-britton?shelf=manga">manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86934326-britton?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86934326-britton?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2582811379" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16496290518892050790">(Minor Spoilers) <br/><br/>I used to believe that manga was a bit too silly for my tastes. American comics can get away with it because they know how to ground their silliness and not lose track of the story at hand. <br/><br/>But then Death Note came along... <br/><br/>Death Note singlehandedly solved any issues I had with manga and is, to this day, the only manga that I can say without a doubt is my favorite and one I will defend until I die. <br/><br/>The series follows Light Yagami, a young high schooler bored with mundane, everyd</span>
  <span id="freeText16496290518892050790" style="display:none">(Minor Spoilers) <br /><br />I used to believe that manga was a bit too silly for my tastes. American comics can get away with it because they know how to ground their silliness and not lose track of the story at hand. <br /><br />But then Death Note came along... <br /><br />Death Note singlehandedly solved any issues I had with manga and is, to this day, the only manga that I can say without a doubt is my favorite and one I will defend until I die. <br /><br />The series follows Light Yagami, a young high schooler bored with mundane, everyday life. But that all changes when he comes across a very strange notebook, dubbed the Death Note, which belongs to a race of old death Gods known as the Shinigami. One particular Shinigami, Ryuk, is also bored and befriends Light over their mutual boredom. You'd expect Ryuk to take Light's soul or something of the sort, but no. Light can have the book and do whatever he wants, as long as he wants with it. If Light dosen't want it anymore, Ryuk will take it and wipe Light's memory of ever encountering it. Light decides to go for something noble and eradicate all crime in the world, all while becoming what he hates and devolves into a megalomaniacal sociopath with a raging God complex who becomes just as, if not more dangerous than the people he hates. <br /><br />Death Note is a clever mix of crime drama and dark fantasy, but is also a meditation on justice, fate, and how a man loses his soul when given power over fate itself. Light Yagami is almost Walter White with a magic book, which might sound negative, but it's really not. Light Yagami is up there with antiheroes (or anti-villains) such as Tony Soprano, Walter White, MacBeth, Pinky Brown, Dexter Morgan, and I can name more. But is more like Frank Underwood in how, while you root for him sometimes, you become more and more disenfranchised with his increasingly immoral acts and you begin to question if you even should even root for him. We also meet such unforgettable characters as Ryuk, Misa, L, Near, Mello, and so much more. <br /><br />Ohba's writing and Takeshi Obata's beautiful art plays with the conventions of the manga medium, showing people that Manga was much more than an over the top, cheeky band of silliness that it can often be. But also shows that manga is an art form, like comics, prose, and everything else. Death Note, for me, is comparable to the early Vertigo works of authors like Alan Moore, Grant Morrison, Peter Milligan, Neil Gaiman, Warren Ellis, etc and how they don't just subvert genre cliches, but also the medium itself and playing with the endless possibilities of the medium at hand, and Ohba takes every opportunity that he/she can to see what they can do with the medium. <br /><br />Death Note, to keep it short, is nothing short of a masterpiece and one of the best mangas I've ever had the pleasure of reading.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16496290518892050790" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3351237713" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3351237713" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1829047703839595329">This is a review of the entire series.<br/><br/>Synopsis: Light Yagami is an ace student with great prospects and he's bored out of his mind. But all that changes when he finds the Death Note, a notebook dropped by a rogue Shinigami, a death god. Any human whose name is written in the notebook dies, and now Light has vowed to use the power of the Death Note to rid the world of evil. But when criminals begin dropping dead, the authorities send the legendary detective L to track down the killer. With L hot </span>
  <span id="freeText1829047703839595329" style="display:none">This is a review of the entire series.<br /><br />Synopsis: Light Yagami is an ace student with great prospects and he's bored out of his mind. But all that changes when he finds the Death Note, a notebook dropped by a rogue Shinigami, a death god. Any human whose name is written in the notebook dies, and now Light has vowed to use the power of the Death Note to rid the world of evil. But when criminals begin dropping dead, the authorities send the legendary detective L to track down the killer. With L hot on his heels, will Light lose sight of his noble goal... or his life?<br /><br />Review: This series is intelligent, dark, full of suspense and makes clever use of metaphorical religious themes and imagery. It’s a look into what happens when great power falls into the hands of a young man named Light. Light is a collected, highly skilled and incredibly smart young man with the powerful urge to make the world a better place. The Death Note gives Light the ability to kill anyone at any time by writing their name down in the notebook and he aims to erase all criminals from the world, as well as innocent people that may try to get in the way of his morally flawed goal.<br /><br />Light becomes corrupted by the power to choose when people die and we are subjected to watching an idealistic young hero slowly reveal himself to be a narcissistic sociopath with a god complex. Light is cunning and charismatic, yet he’s also petty and spiteful. You'll find yourself rooting for him as often as you'll find yourself hating him.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1829047703839595329" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3029125748" />
    <a title="Jpage20" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/102370130-jpage20"><img alt="Jpage20" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3029125748?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jpage20" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jpage20" href="/user/show/102370130-jpage20">Jpage20</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3029125748&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3029125748" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14010898595136957966">The resolution is coming up very soon, and Near, L's "successor" instinctively knows that Light Yagami is Kira, playing the role of three different people: Kira, L, and Light Yagami in the Police Task Force. Near decides to travel to Japan after challenging L to finding Kira first. L, or Kira, confidently accepts the challenge, not knowing what Near had already been doing. Mikami, Kira's right hand man, was being spied on by Near's secret agent to find out about the murder weapon. The infiltrati</span>
  <span id="freeText14010898595136957966" style="display:none">The resolution is coming up very soon, and Near, L's "successor" instinctively knows that Light Yagami is Kira, playing the role of three different people: Kira, L, and Light Yagami in the Police Task Force. Near decides to travel to Japan after challenging L to finding Kira first. L, or Kira, confidently accepts the challenge, not knowing what Near had already been doing. Mikami, Kira's right hand man, was being spied on by Near's secret agent to find out about the murder weapon. The infiltration was successful and Near was able to find out a notebook called the Death Note was the real murder weapon and how it was used. The only thing left to do was make it obvious to the whole world that Light Yagami was the real Kira, and stop him once and for all, but how, was the real question. As stated in the other reviews, the art style is no different and very detailed. I really enjoyed this volume and finished it in a few hours wanting to also read the last book extremely fast. The central conflict of this volume was, well, what is stated in the summary basically. Near had to find a way to make Kira show his true face in front of the world to see. Recommendation is obviously for everybody because of how brilliant the pacing and character development is.</span>

          </span>

A lot of repetition brings the reader to understand that this finale is a battle of pride and that there is only one satisfying ending for each</span>
  <span id="freeText9728261432326972446" style="display:none">With Light Yagami now between a rock and a hard place, coincidences give him a hand to put him in a favourable position to concoct his latest and final plan to eliminate all those who are in his way from establishing the New World he envisioned as Kira.<br /><br />The volume essentially sets up the circumstances and setting that will lead to the inevitable showdown. A lot of repetition brings the reader to understand that this finale is a battle of pride and that there is only one satisfying ending for each of the concerned characters.<br /><br />A lot of what made this series great is overshadowed by the events that are unfolding and the story loses its supernatural touch to focus on a more intimate battle that takes center stage.<br /><br />Yours truly,<br /><br />Lashaan | Blogger and Book Reviewer<br />Official blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://bookidote.com/">https://bookidote.com/</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5170266001202249200">In Death Note 11 Near suspects light of being Kira. He does not want to have any doubts about light so he flies to japan to get more evidence. Near just wants to expose light as the killer. He doesn't want to stop Kira. The genres it would fit under is manga, scifi, horror, superhero, crime mystery, political and contemporary life. The books art style is black and white. It has thin lines and little shading. The setting of the story is unique. The story and the characters are also unique. The pl</span>
  <span id="freeText5170266001202249200" style="display:none">In Death Note 11 Near suspects light of being Kira. He does not want to have any doubts about light so he flies to japan to get more evidence. Near just wants to expose light as the killer. He doesn't want to stop Kira. The genres it would fit under is manga, scifi, horror, superhero, crime mystery, political and contemporary life. The books art style is black and white. It has thin lines and little shading. The setting of the story is unique. The story and the characters are also unique. The plot of the story is different from other stories. I would recommend this book. It has a great story and the book continues the story very well.<br /></span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('054B1PvdWBseOMOobS4pqRpOvcg7PQat7HYjlftN5OawQ53HFInRinJxzhsLOVz88+RzPdhZQEGPdGcp3zg8qw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JvoxrVqMEQP39Tc/lb0g7OYYASm3Ve1y0RB1TJw390tFJ62+tdiYkpu8OozzqlW5D7LP3FQxq56yEjHwuEIvBg==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13251308476048540208">Tsugumi Ōba (Profile in Japanese: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19876928.______' title='大場 つぐみ' rel='nofollow noopener'>大場 つぐみ</a>), born in Tokyo, Japan, is a writer best known for the manga Death Note. His/her real identity is a closely guarded secret. As stated by the profile placed at the beginning of each Death Note manga, Ōba collects teacups and develops manga plots while holding his knees on a chair, similar to a habit of L, one of the main characters of the series.<br/><br/>There is spe</span>
  <span id="freeText13251308476048540208" style="display:none">Tsugumi Ōba (Profile in Japanese: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19876928.______" title="大場 つぐみ" rel="nofollow noopener">大場 つぐみ</a>), born in Tokyo, Japan, is a writer best known for the manga Death Note. His/her real identity is a closely guarded secret. As stated by the profile placed at the beginning of each Death Note manga, Ōba collects teacups and develops manga plots while holding his knees on a chair, similar to a habit of L, one of the main characters of the series.<br /><br />There is speculation that Tsugumi Ōba is a pen name and that he is really Hiroshi Gamō. Pointing out that in Bakuman the main character's uncle was a one-hit wonder manga artist who worked on a gag super hero manga, very similar to Gamō and Tottemo! Luckyman in all aspects. Also that the storyboards drawn by Ōba greatly resemble Tottemo! Luckyman in style.</span>
